    30	const MASK64 = 0xffffffffffffffffn
    31	
    32	function rotl(x: bigint, k: bigint): bigint {
    33	  return ((x << k) | (x >> (64n - k))) & 0xffffffffffffffffn
    34	}
    35	
    36	function wrappingMul(x: bigint, y: bigint) {
    37	  return (x * y) & MASK64
    38	}
    39	
    40	// xoroshiro128**
    41	export function xoroshiro128(state: bigint) {
    42	  return function () {
    43	    let s0 = BigInt(state & MASK64)
    44	    let s1 = BigInt((state >> 64n) & MASK64)
    45	
    46	    const result = wrappingMul(rotl(wrappingMul(s0, 5n), 7n), 9n)
    47	
    48	    s1 ^= s0
    49	    s0 = (rotl(s0, 24n) ^ s1 ^ (s1 << 16n)) & MASK64
    50	    s1 = rotl(s1, 37n)
    51	
    52	    state = (s1 << 64n) | s0
    53	
    54	    return result
    55	  }
    56	}
    57

   303	
   304	/*
   305	 * NOTES ABOUT 0x88 MOVE GENERATION ALGORITHM
   306	 * ----------------------------------------------------------------------------
   307	 * From https://github.com/jhlywa/chess.js/issues/230
   308	 *
   309	 * A lot of people are confused when they first see the internal representation
   310	 * of chess.js. It uses the 0x88 Move Generation Algorithm which internally
   311	 * stores the board as an 8x16 array. This is purely for efficiency but has a
   312	 * couple of interesting benefits:
   313	 *
   314	 * 1. 0x88 offers a very inexpensive "off the board" check. Bitwise AND (&) any
   315	 *    square with 0x88, if the result is non-zero then the square is off the
   316	 *    board. For example, assuming a knight square A8 (0 in 0x88 notation),
   317	 *    there are 8 possible directions in which the knight can move. These
   318	 *    directions are relative to the 8x16 board and are stored in the
   319	 *    PIECE_OFFSETS map. One possible move is A8 - 18 (up one square, and two
   320	 *    squares to the left - which is off the board). 0 - 18 = -18 & 0x88 = 0x88
   321	 *    (because of two-complement representation of -18). The non-zero result
   322	 *    means the square is off the board and the move is illegal. Take the
   323	 *    opposite move (from A8 to C7), 0 + 18 = 18 & 0x88 = 0. A result of zero
   324	 *    means the square is on the board.
   325	 *
   326	 * 2. The relative distance (or difference) between two squares on a 8x16 board
   327	 *    is unique and can be used to inexpensively determine if a piece on a
   328	 *    square can attack any other arbitrary square. For example, let's see if a
   329	 *    pawn on E7 can attack E2. The difference between E7 (20) - E2 (100) is
   330	 *    -80. We add 119 to make the ATTACKS array index non-negative (because the
   331	 *    worst case difference is A8 - H1 = -119). The ATTACKS array contains a
   332	 *    bitmask of pieces that can attack from that distance and direction.
   333	 *    ATTACKS[-80 + 119=39] gives us 24 or 0b11000 in binary. Look at the
   334	 *    PIECE_MASKS map to determine the mask for a given piece type. In our pawn
   335	 *    example, we would check to see if 24 & 0x1 is non-zero, which it is
   336	 *    not. So, naturally, a pawn on E7 can't attack a piece on E2. However, a
   337	 *    rook can since 24 & 0x8 is non-zero. The only thing left to check is that
   338	 *    there are no blocking pieces between E7 and E2. That's where the RAYS
   339	 *    array comes in. It provides an offset (in this case 16) to add to E7 (20)
   340	 *    to check for blocking pieces. E7 (20) + 16 = E6 (36) + 16 = E5 (52) etc.
   341	 */
   342	
   343	// prettier-ignore
   344	// eslint-disable-next-line

   407	const PIECE_MASKS = { p: 0x1, n: 0x2, b: 0x4, r: 0x8, q: 0x10, k: 0x20 }

   446	// Extracts the zero-based rank of an 0x88 square.
   447	function rank(square: number): number {
   448	  return square >> 4
   449	}
   450	
   451	// Extracts the zero-based file of an 0x88 square.
   452	function file(square: number): number {
   453	  return square & 0xf
   454	}
   455	
   456	function isDigit(c: string): boolean {
   457	  return '0123456789'.indexOf(c) !== -1
   458	}
   459	
   460	// Converts a 0x88 square to algebraic notation.
   461	function algebraic(square: number): Square {
   462	  const f = file(square)
   463	  const r = rank(square)
   464	  return ('abcdefgh'.substring(f, f + 1) +
   465	    '87654321'.substring(r, r + 1)) as Square
   466	}

   468	function swapColor(color: Color): Color {
   469	  return color === WHITE ? BLACK : WHITE
   470	}
   471	
   472	export function validateFen(fen: string): { ok: boolean; error?: string } {
   473	  // 1st criterion: 6 space-seperated fields?
   474	  const tokens = fen.split(/\s+/)
   475	  if (tokens.length !== 6) {
   476	    return {
   477	      ok: false,
   478	      error: 'Invalid FEN: must contain six space-delimited fields',
   479	    }
   480	  }
   481	
   482	  // 2nd criterion: move number field is a integer value > 0?
   483	  const moveNumber = parseInt(tokens[5], 10)
   484	  if (isNaN(moveNumber) || moveNumber <= 0) {
   485	    return {
   486	      ok: false,
   487	      error: 'Invalid FEN: move number must be a positive integer',
   488	    }
   489	  }
   490	
   491	  // 3rd criterion: half move counter is an integer >= 0?
   492	  const halfMoves = parseInt(tokens[4], 10)
   493	  if (isNaN(halfMoves) || halfMoves < 0) {
   494	    return {
   495	      ok: false,
   496	      error:
   497	        'Invalid FEN: half move counter number must be a non-negative integer',
   498	    }
   499	  }
   500	
   501	  // 4th criterion: 4th field is a valid e.p.-string?
   502	  if (!/^(-|[abcdefgh][36])$/.test(tokens[3])) {
   503	    return { ok: false, error: 'Invalid FEN: en-passant square is invalid' }
   504	  }
   505	
   506	  // 5th criterion: 3th field is a valid castle-string?
   507	  if (/[^kKqQ-]/.test(tokens[2])) {
   508	    return { ok: false, error: 'Invalid FEN: castling availability is invalid' }
   509	  }
   510	
   511	  // 6th criterion: 2nd field is "w" (white) or "b" (black)?
   512	  if (!/^(w|b)$/.test(tokens[1])) {
   513	    return { ok: false, error: 'Invalid FEN: side-to-move is invalid' }
   514	  }
   515	
   516	  // 7th criterion: 1st field contains 8 rows?
   517	  const rows = tokens[0].split('/')
   518	  if (rows.length !== 8) {
   519	    return {
   520	      ok: false,
   521	      error: "Invalid FEN: piece data does not contain 8 '/'-delimited rows",
   522	    }
   523	  }
   524	
   525	  // 8th criterion: every row is valid?
   526	  for (let i = 0; i < rows.length; i++) {
   527	    // check for right sum of fields AND not two numbers in succession
   528	    let sumFields = 0
   529	    let previousWasNumber = false
   530	
   531	    for (let k = 0; k < rows[i].length; k++) {
   532	      if (isDigit(rows[i][k])) {
   533	        if (previousWasNumber) {
   534	          return {
   535	            ok: false,
   536	            error: 'Invalid FEN: piece data is invalid (consecutive number)',
   537	          }
   538	        }
   539	        sumFields += parseInt(rows[i][k], 10)
   540	        previousWasNumber = true
   541	      } else {
   542	        if (!/^[prnbqkPRNBQK]$/.test(rows[i][k])) {
   543	          return {
   544	            ok: false,
   545	            error: 'Invalid FEN: piece data is invalid (invalid piece)',
   546	          }
   547	        }
   548	        sumFields += 1
   549	        previousWasNumber = false
   550	      }
   551	    }
   552	    if (sumFields !== 8) {
   553	      return {
   554	        ok: false,
   555	        error: 'Invalid FEN: piece data is invalid (too many squares in rank)',
   556	      }
   557	    }
   558	  }
   559	
   560	  // 9th criterion: is en-passant square legal?
   561	  if (
   562	    (tokens[3][1] == '3' && tokens[1] == 'w') ||
   563	    (tokens[3][1] == '6' && tokens[1] == 'b')
   564	  ) {
   565	    return { ok: false, error: 'Invalid FEN: illegal en-passant square' }
   566	  }
   567	
   568	  // 10th criterion: does chess position contain exact two kings?
   569	  const kings = [
   570	    { color: 'white', regex: /K/g },
   571	    { color: 'black', regex: /k/g },
   572	  ]
   573	
   574	  for (const { color, regex } of kings) {
   575	    if (!regex.test(tokens[0])) {
   576	      return { ok: false, error: `Invalid FEN: missing ${color} king` }
   577	    }
   578	
   579	    if ((tokens[0].match(regex) || []).length > 1) {
   580	      return { ok: false, error: `Invalid FEN: too many ${color} kings` }
   581	    }
   582	  }
   583	
   584	  // 11th criterion: are any pawns on the first or eighth rows?
   585	  if (
   586	    Array.from(rows[0] + rows[7]).some((char) => char.toUpperCase() === 'P')
   587	  ) {
   588	    return {
   589	      ok: false,
   590	      error: 'Invalid FEN: some pawns are on the edge rows',
   591	    }
   592	  }
   593	
   594	  return { ok: true }
   595	}

   597	// this function is used to uniquely identify ambiguous moves
   598	function getDisambiguator(move: InternalMove, moves: InternalMove[]): string {
   599	  const from = move.from
   600	  const to = move.to

  1158	      return
  1159	    }
  1160

I found the issue! Looking at the code and the debug output, the problem is that after the pawn move `h2h4`, the `_epSquare` gets cleared by the `_updateEnPassantSquare()` method because it checks if there are valid pawns that can capture en passant.

However, there's an even more fundamental issue: in the `fen()` method, when `forceEnpassantSquare` is `true`, the code should not validate whether the en passant capture is legal. It should simply include the en passant square regardless of validation.

The current logic in the `fen()` method (lines 871-910) is:
1. If `_epSquare !== EMPTY`
2. If `forceEnpassantSquare` is true, set `epSquare` directly
3. If `forceEnpassantSquare` is false, validate if en passant is possible

The issue is that the validation logic (lines 875-909) is also checking if the en passant capture leaves the king in check, which is too restrictive for the intended behavior of `forceEnpassantSquare`.

function algebraic(square) {
    if (square === -1) return '"'"'-'"'"';
    const f = square & 0xf;
    const r = (square >> 4); // Convert 0x88 rank to algebraic notation

@@ -0,0 +1,40 @@
+const { Chess } = require('./dist/cjs/chess.js');
+
+// Extract the algebraic function from the built chess module
+function algebraic(square) {
+    if (square === -1) return '-';
+    const f = square & 0xf;
+    const r = (square >> 4); // Convert 0x88 rank to algebraic notation 
+    // 0x88 squares: rank 0 = a8-h8, rank 1 = a7-h7, etc.
+    // Algebraic notation: rank 7 = a8-h8, rank 6 = a7-h7, etc.
+    const algebraicRank = 7 - r;
+    return 'abcdefgh'.substring(f, f + 1) + '87654321'.substring(algebraicRank, algebraicRank + 1);
+}
+
+const chess = new Chess('rnb1kbn1/p1p1pp2/PpPp2qr/5Pp1/8/R1P4p/1PK1P1PP/1NBQ1BNR b - - 0 1');
+console.log('Initial FEN:', chess.fen());
+
+// Check e5 move details
+const moves = chess.moves({ verbose: true });
+const e5move = moves.find(m => m.from === 'e7' && m.to === 'e5');
+console.log('e5 move details:', {
+    from: e5move?.from,
+    to: e5move?.to,
+    flags: e5move?.flags,
+    isBigPawn: e5move?.isBigPawn(),
+    piece: e5move?.piece
+});
+

+const { Chess } = require('./dist/cjs/chess.js');
+
+// Test the exact position from the test file
+const fen = 'rnb1kbn1/p1p1pp2/PpPp2qr/5Pp1/8/R1P4p/1PK1P1PP/1NBQ1BNR b - - 0 1';
+const chess = new Chess(fen);

+console.log(chess.ascii());

+const moves = chess.moves({ verbose: true });
+moves.forEach(m => {
+    if (m.from === 'e7' && m.to === 'e5') {
+        console.log('Found e5 move:', m);
+        console.log('Flags:', m.flags);
+        console.log('isBigPawn:', m.isBigPawn());
+    }
+});
+
+// Make the pawn move
+chess.move('e5');
+
+console.log('\nAfter move e5:');
+console.log('_epSquare:', chess._epSquare);
+console.log('_intendedEpSquare:', chess._intendedEpSquare);
+console.log('Turn:', chess._turn);
+
+// The pawn moved from e7 to e5 - this should create en passant at e6
+// Check what the intended ep square should be
+console.log('\nMove analysis:');
+console.log('Pawn moves from e7 (16*1 + 4 = 20) to e5 (16*3 + 4 = 52)');
+console.log('Big pawn move, so intendedEpSquare should be e6 (16*2 + 4 = 36)');
+
+console.log('\nChecking pawns adjacent to the landing square (e5):');
+const e5 = 52; // 0x88 for e5
+const leftSquare = e5 - 1; // d5
+const rightSquare = e5 + 1; // f5
+
+console.log('Square left of e5 (d5):', leftSquare);
+console.log('Square right of e5 (f5):', rightSquare);
+
+// Check if there are pawns that could capture
+function checkSquare(sq) {
+    const piece = chess._board[sq];
+    return piece ? `${piece.color}${piece.type}` : 'empty';
+}
+
+console.log('Left square (d5):', checkSquare(leftSquare));
+console.log('Right square (f5):', checkSquare(rightSquare));
+
+// Rebuild and test
+console.log('\nShould _epSquare be set to 36 (e6)?');
+console.log('There IS a white pawn at f5 that could capture en passant from e6');
